## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv_dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The equation of motion typically involves restoring forces (functions of x), damping terms (functions of v), and possibly driving forces (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Cubic nonlinear oscillator (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonic driving force)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order Duffing)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (mixed nonlinear coupling)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (combined nonlinearities)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear restoring force → term proportional to -x (simple harmonic behavior)
- Cubic position dependence → x**3 term indicates Duffing-type hardening or softening spring nonlinearity
- Velocity-proportional term → c*v represents linear viscous damping or energy injection
- Velocity times position squared → (1 - x**2)*v structure indicates Van der Pol-type self-sustained oscillation
- Periodic driving → sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms represent external harmonic forcing
- Odd-power restoring forces → x, x**3, x**5 preserve symmetry of the oscillator potential
- Even-power position terms → x**2 breaks symmetry, indicates asymmetric potential well
- Nonlinear damping → v**3 or v*|v| indicates amplitude-dependent energy dissipation
- Product x*v terms → indicate phase-space-dependent forces or nonlinear coupling between position and velocity
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence of t suggests driven or parametric excitation
